05/01/2021, 16:14 - Basu: Secret image sharing (SIS) with small-sized shadow images has many benefits, such as saving storage space, improving transmission time, and achieving information hiding. When adjacent pixel values in an image are similar to each other, the secret image will be leaked when all random factors of an SIS scheme are utilized for achieving small sizes of shadow images. Most of the studies in this area suffer from an inevitable problem: auxiliary encryption is crucial in ensuring the security of those schemes. In this paper, an SIS scheme with small-sized shadow images based on the Chinese remainder theorem (CRT) is proposed. The size of shadow images can be reduced to nearly 1/k of the original secret image. By adding random bits to binary representations of the random factors in the CRT, auxiliary encryption is not necessary for this scheme. Additionally, reasonable modifications of the random factors make it possible to incorporate all advantages of the CRT as well, including a (k, n) threshold, lossless recovery, and low computation complexity. Analyses and experiments are provided to demonstrate the effectiveness of the proposed scheme.

09/01/2021, 11:48 - Basu: 2nd ka production system 

A production systems is a forward-chaining reasoning system that uses rules of a certain form called production rules as its representation of general knowledge” In other words, production systems reason in the “forward” direction, that is, from premises to conclusions. This is in contrast to backward-chaining systems (such as prolog) which start from the conclusions and try to reason backwards through the premises.

multinational software company conducts an interview for the post of software engineer. A There are certain number of appointments from 0 to 91. The appointments are given to candidates using the hashing function h(k)=k mod 91, where k is the number formed from the last three digits on the call letter. What are the appointments assigned by the hashing function to the candidates having the following last three number on their call letter? 102, 999, 138, 378, 375, 456. Check the free appointment, if any appointment collides

for (k in 1:500) { 
    n = k 
    i = 1 
    s = 0 
  
    while (i < n) { 
      if (n %% i == 0) { 
        s = s + i 
      } 
      i = i + 1 
    } 
    if (s == n) { 
      print(paste(n,"is a perfect number")) 
    }  
    k=k+1 
    }

s = 1

}

gcd <- function (a,b) {
      if(b == 0){
    return (a)
  }
  gcd(b, a %% b)
}
print(gcd(15,30))

n=as.integer(n);
last_no=n%%10
first_no=n
while(n>=10)
{
  n=n/10
}
first_no=n
sum=first_no+last_no

#10
nterms = as.integer(readline(prompt="How many terms? "))
n1 = 0
n2 = 1
count = 2
if(nterms <= 0) {
  print("Plese enter a positive integer")
} else {
  if(nterms == 1) {
    print("Fibonacci sequence:")
    print(n1)
  } else {
    print("Fibonacci sequence:")
    print(n1)
    print(n2)
    while(count < nterms) {
      nth = n1 + n2
      print(nth)
      # update values
      n1 = n2
      n2 = nth
      count = count + 1
    }
  }
}

#11
n = as.integer(readline(prompt = "Enter a number :"))
rev = 0
while (n > 0) {
  r = n %% 10
  rev = rev * 10 + r
  n = n %/% 10
}
print(paste("Reverse number is :", rev))

#5
diamond <- function(max) {

    #Upper triangle
    space <- max - 1
    for (i in 0:(max - 1)) {
        for (j in 0:space) cat(" ")
        for (j in 0:i) cat("* ")
        cat("\n")
        space <- space - 1
    }

    # Lower triangle
    space = 1;
    for (i in (max - 1):1) {
        for (j in 0:space) cat(" ")
        for (j in 0:(i - 1)) cat("* ")
        cat("\n")
        space <- space + 1
    }
}

diamond(5)

#6
{
    n <- as.integer(readline(prompt = "Input number of rows: "))
    k <- n - 1
    for (i in 0:(n - 1)) {
        for(j in 0:k) cat(" ")
        for(j in 0:i) cat(j + 1)
        j <- i
        while (j>0) {
            cat(j)
            j<-j-1
            
        }
        cat("\n")
        k<-k-1
    }
}
#7
{
    n <- as.integer(readline(prompt = "Input a number :"))
    x <- n
    prod <- x%%10
    x <- x%/%10
    while (x>0) 
    {
        prod <- prod*(x%%10)
        x <- x%/%10
    }
    cat(paste0("The product of digit of ",n," is: ",prod)) 
}

#8
{
    n <- as.integer(readline(prompt = "Input the base: "))
    m <- as.integer(readline(prompt = "Input the exponent: "))
    prod <- n
    for (i in 2:m) {
        prod <- prod*n
    }
    cat(paste0(n," ^ ",m," = ",prod))  
}

#9
{
    divisible = function()
    {
        cat("Numbers Between 100 and 200, divisible by 9: \n")
        sum <-0
        for (i in 100:200) 
        {
            if(i%%9==0)
            {
                cat(paste0(i," "))
                sum <-sum + i
            }
        }
        cat(paste0("\n The sum: ",sum))
    }
    divisible()  
}

#10
{
    n <- as.integer(readline(prompt = "Input number of term to display: "))
    fib = function(m)
    {
        cat(paste0("Here is the fibonacci series upto",m," terms:\n"))
        x<-0
        y<-1
        cat(" 0 1 ")
        for (i in 3:m) {
            z<-y
            y<-x+y
            x<-z
            cat(paste0(y," "))
        }
    }
    fib(10)  
}

#11
{
    n <- as.integer(readline(prompt = "Input the value for the nth term: "))
    series <- function(m)
    {
        sum <- 0
        for (i in 1:m) {
            sum1 <- 1
            cat(1)
            if(i>1)
                for (j in 2:i) {
                    sum1 <- sum1 + j
                    cat(paste0("+",j))
                    
                }
            cat(paste0(" = ",sum1,"\n"))
            sum<-sum+sum1
        }
        cat(paste0("The sum of the above series is: ",sum))
    }
    series(5)
}

24/04/2021, 21:09 - Nibba UltraPro: #1
{
  fbci = as.integer(readline(prompt = "How many terms?"))
  
  n1 = 0
  n2 = 1
  
  count = 2
  
  if(fbci <= 0){
    print("Please enter a positive value!")
  }else {
    if(fbci == 1) {
      print("Fibonacci Sequence: ")
      print(n1)
    }else{
      print("Fibonacci sequence:")
      print(n1)
      print(n2)
      while (count < fbci) {
        nth = n1 + n2
        print(nth)
        n1 = n2
        n2 = nth
        count = count + 1
      }
    }
  } 
}

CREATE TABLE SalesPerson (
  SalesPersonNumber INTEGER PRIMARY KEY,
  SalesPersonName TEXT NOT NULL,

  YearHire INTEGER NOT NULL,
  OfficeNumber INTEGER NOT NULL
);
CREATE TABLE Customer (
  CustomerNumber INTEGER PRIMARY KEY,
  CustomerName TEXT NOT NULL,
  SalesPersonNumber TEXT NOT NULL,
  HeadQuarteCity TEXT NOT NULL
);
CREATE TABLE CustomerEmployee (
  CustomerNumber INTEGER PRIMARY KEY,
  EmployeeNumber INTEGER NOT NULL,
  EmployeeName TEXT NOT NULL,
  Title TEXT NOT NULL
);
CREATE TABLE Product (
  ProductNumber INTEGER PRIMARY KEY,
  ProductName TEXT NOT NULL,
  UnitPrice INTEGER NOT NULL
);
CREATE TABLE Sales (
  SalesPersonNumber INTEGER PRIMARY KEY,
  ProductNumber INTEGER NOT NULL,
  Quantity INTEGER NOT NULL
);
CREATE TABLE Office (
  OfficeNumber INTEGER PRIMARY KEY,
  Telephone INTEGER NOT NULL,
  SIze INTEGER NOT NULL
);
